	function opt_log_link_click(link_id,url){
		jQuery.post(opt_ajaxurl,{'action' : 'opt_links_tracking',

		},200);	
	}

		}
	}

	function opt_form_close(link_id,split_test_item_id){
		
		jQuery.ajax(opt_ajaxurl,{'dataType' : 'json',
							'data': {'action' : 'opt_forms_tracking',
									'visitor_cookie' : dwpc_visitor_id,
									'impression_id' : dwpc_impression_id,
									'forms_id' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('form_id'),
									'links_id' : link_id,
									'tracking_type' : 'Close',
									'split_test_item_id':split_test_item_id}
							});
		jQuery('#optin_link_overlay'+link_id).fadeOut();
		$opt_cur_form_container.fadeOut();
		

	}
	
	function opt_form_onload(link_id){
		jQuery(document).ready(function(){
			jQuery('#optin_link_form_name' + link_id).keypress(function(e){
				
				if ((e.which && e.which == 13) || (e.keyCode && e.keyCode == 13)) {
					jQuery('#optin_link_button_text' + link_id).click();
					return false;
				} else {
					return true;
				}	
			});
			jQuery('#optin_link_form_email' + link_id).keypress(function(e){
				lastEvent = e;
				if ((e.which && e.which == 13) || (e.keyCode && e.keyCode == 13)) {
					jQuery('#optin_link_button_text' + link_id).click();
					return false;
				} else {
					return true;
				}	
			});	
		});	
	}
	
	function opt_form_submit(link_id){
		
		var clicked = $opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked');
		if(typeof(clicked) == 'undefined'){$opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked',true);}else if(clicked){return;}
		
		$form_processing = jQuery('#optin_link_form_processing' + link_id);
		$form_success = jQuery('#optin_link_form_success' + link_id);
		$form_error = jQuery('#optin_link_form_error' + link_id);
		$form = jQuery('#optin_link_form' + link_id);
		$form_success_image = jQuery('#optin_link_success_image' + link_id);
		
		$form_redirect_link = jQuery('#optin_link_redirect_text' + link_id);
		
		$email = jQuery('#optin_link_form_email'+ link_id);
		$name = jQuery('#optin_link_form_name'+ link_id);
		
		var valid_form_details = true;
		
		var customs = [];
		
		valid_form_details = valid_form_details && ($name.val() !== "");
		valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_rgxemvd($email.val());
			
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_phone_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_phone_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('phone');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_gender_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_gender_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('gender');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_dob_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_dob_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('dob');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_address1_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_address1_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('address1');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_address2_'+link_id)){
			customs.push('address2');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_city_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_city_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('city');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_state_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_state_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('state');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_zip_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_zip_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('zip');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_country_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_country_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('country');
		}
		
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_custom1_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_custom1_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('custom1');
		}
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_custom2_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_custom2_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('custom2');
		}
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_custom3_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_custom3_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('custom3');
		}
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_custom4_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_custom4_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('custom4');
		}
		if(opt_element_exists('opt_custom_custom5_'+link_id)){
			valid_form_details = valid_form_details && opt_check_elem('opt_custom_custom5_'+link_id);	
			customs.push('custom5');
		}
			
		if(!valid_form_details ){
			$form_error.show();
			$opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked',false);
		}else{
			$form_error.hide();
			$form_processing.fadeIn();
			window.setInterval(function(){var _this = jQuery('#optin_link_process_dots' + link_id);var num = _this.data('num');if(typeof(num)=='undefined'){num=0;}var dots='';for(var i =0;i<num;i++){dots+='.';}_this.text(dots);var dir = _this.data('dir');if(typeof(dir)=='undefined'){dir=1;}if(num > 3){dir = -1;}if(num < 0){dir = 1;}num += dir; _this.data('num',num); _this.data('dir',dir);},250);
			var data = {'dataType' : 'json',
							'data': {'action' : 'opt_create_lead',
									'visitor_cookie' : dwpc_visitor_id,
									'impression_id' : dwpc_impression_id,
									'forms_id' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('form_id'),
									'links_id' : link_id,
									'link_tracking_id' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('opt_link_tracking_id'),
									'email' : $email.val(),
									'name' : $name.val(),
									'secured_page' : opt_secured_page_id },
						'success' : function(data,textStatus,jqXHR){
							var redirect_mult = 1;
							if(typeof(data['custom_forms']) !== 'undefined'){
								if(typeof($name.val()) == 'undefined'){
									var name = ' ';
								}else{
									name = $name.val();	
								}
								jQuery('<iframe src="'+opt_cf_href+'&optinlinks_email='+rawurlencode($email.val())+'&optinlinks_name='+rawurlencode(name)+'&dwpc_impression_id='+dwpc_impression_id+'&optinlink_id='+link_id+'&optinlinks_form_html=1"></iframe>').appendTo('body');
								redirect_mult = 2;
							}
							
							$opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked',false);
							if(opt_ajax_options(data)){return;}
							
							$form.hide();
							$form_success.show();
							
							opt_redir_url = data['redir_url'];
							
							opt_set_cookie(data);
							
							
							window.setTimeout(function(){
								window.location = opt_redir_url;
							},3*1000*redirect_mult);
						}};
			
			for(var i = 0;i<customs.length;i++){
				var val = opt_find_value('opt_custom_'+customs[i]+'_'+link_id);
				data.data[customs[i]] = val;	
			}
			
			jQuery.ajax(opt_ajaxurl, data);	
			
		}
	}
	
	function opt_set_cookie(data){
		var expires = new Date();
		expires.setTime(expires.getTime() + (360 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
		document.cookie = data['cookie_name'] + '=' + data['cookie'] + '; expires=' + expires.toUTCString() + '; path=/; domain=adriennesmith.net';
	}
	
	function opt_ajax_new_tab(data){
		opt_set_cookie(data);
		
		if(typeof($form_waiting)!=='undefined'){
			$form_waiting.hide();
		}
		
		$form.hide();
		$form_success.show();

		// Some fancy JS to get just the text in the base element - not any children
		var linkText = $form_redirect_link.contents().filter(function(){
			return this.nodeType == 3;
		})[0].nodeValue
		if (linkText != null && linkText.trim() == DEFAULT_TEXT) {
			$form_redirect_link.text('Click here to go to your special offer!');
		}
		$form_redirect_link.css('cursor','pointer');
								
		$form_success_image.attr('src',opt_images_href + 'close.png');
		$form_success_image.css('cursor','pointer');
		$form_success_image.click(function(){
			opt_form_close($opt_cur_form_container.data('link_id'),$opt_cur_form_container.data('split_test_item_id'));
		});
								
		$form_redirect_link.click(function(){
			opt_form_close($opt_cur_form_container.data('link_id'),$opt_cur_form_container.data('split_test_item_id'));
			window.open(data['redir_url'],'_blank');	
		});
	}
	function opt_ajax_no_redirect(data){
		opt_set_cookie(data);
		
		if(typeof($form_waiting)!=='undefined'){
			$form_waiting.hide();
		}
		
		$form.hide();
		$form_success.show();

		// Some fancy JS to get just the text in the base element - not any children
		var linkText = $form_redirect_link.contents().filter(function(){
			return this.nodeType == 3;
		})[0].nodeValue
		if (linkText != null && linkText.trim() == DEFAULT_TEXT) {
			$form_redirect_link.text("Thanks for subscribing!");
		}
								 
		$form_success_image.attr('src',opt_images_href + 'close.png');
		$form_success_image.css('cursor','pointer');
		$form_success_image.click(function(){
			opt_form_close($opt_cur_form_container.data('link_id'),$opt_cur_form_container.data('split_test_item_id'));
		});
	}
	function opt_ajax_double(data){
		$opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie', data['cookie']);
		$opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie_name', data['cookie_name']);
		opt_redir_url = data['redir_url'];
		$form_waiting = jQuery('#optin_link_form_waiting'+$opt_cur_form_container.data('link_id')).show();
		$form.hide();
		
		if(typeof(data['no_thanks']) !== 'undefined'){
			if(typeof(data['optin_no_redirect']) !== 'undefined'){
				opt_ajax_no_redirect(data);
				return true;
			}else if(typeof(data['optin_open_in_new_tab']) !== 'undefined'){
				opt_ajax_new_tab(data);
				return true;
			}else{
				
				$form_waiting.hide();
				$form_success.show();
				
				var expires = new Date();
				expires.setTime(expires.getTime() + (360 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
				document.cookie = $opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie_name') + '=' + $opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie') + '; expires=' + expires.toUTCString() + '; path=/; domain=adriennesmith.net';
			
				window.setTimeout(function(){
					window.location = opt_redir_url;
				},3*1000);		
			}
			return true;
		}
		
		var opt_interval_id;
		var check_lead_success = function(CHdata,textStatus,jqXHR){
			if(typeof(CHdata['fail']) !== 'undefined'){return;}
			
			window.clearInterval(opt_interval_id);
			if(typeof(data['optin_no_redirect']) !== 'undefined'){
				opt_ajax_no_redirect(data);
				return true;
			}else if(typeof(data['optin_open_in_new_tab']) !== 'undefined'){
				opt_ajax_new_tab(data);
				return true;
			}else{
				
				$form_waiting.hide();
				$form_success.show();
				
				var expires = new Date();
				expires.setTime(expires.getTime() + (360 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
				document.cookie = $opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie_name') + '=' + $opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie') + '; expires=' + expires.toUTCString() + '; path=/; domain=adriennesmith.net';
			
				window.setTimeout(function(){
					window.location = opt_redir_url;
				},3*1000);		
			}
			
			
		}
		
		opt_interval_id = window.setInterval(function(){
			jQuery.ajax(opt_ajaxurl,{'dataType' : 'json',
								'data': {'action' : 'opt_check_lead',
										'cookie' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('cookie')},
								'success' : check_lead_success});	
		},5*1000);
		return;
	}
	function opt_ajax_options(data){
		
		if(typeof(data['error']) !== 'undefined' ){
			if(data['error'] === 'invalid_email'){
				$form_processing.hide();
				$form_error.show();
				return true;
			}else{
				alert(data['error']);	
				return true;
			}	
		}
		
		
		
		if(typeof(data['double_optin']) !== 'undefined'){
			opt_ajax_double(data);
			return true;
		}else if(typeof(data['optin_no_redirect']) !== 'undefined'){
			opt_ajax_no_redirect(data);
			return true;
		}else if(typeof(data['optin_open_in_new_tab']) !== 'undefined'){
			opt_ajax_new_tab(data);
			return true;
		}
		
		return false;
	}
	
	function opt_form_no_thanks(link_id){
		
		var clicked = $opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked');
		if(typeof(clicked) == 'undefined'){$opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked',true);}else if(clicked){return;}
		
		$form_processing = jQuery('#optin_link_form_processing' + link_id);
		$form_success = jQuery('#optin_link_form_success' + link_id);
		$form_error = jQuery('#optin_link_form_error' + link_id);
		$form = jQuery('#optin_link_form' + link_id);
		$form_success_image = jQuery('#optin_link_success_image' + link_id);
		
		$form_redirect_link = jQuery('#optin_link_redirect_text' + link_id);
		
		$email = jQuery('#optin_link_form_email'+ link_id);
		$name = jQuery('#optin_link_form_name'+ link_id);
		
		if( false ){
			$form_error.show();
		}else{
			$form_error.hide();
			$form_processing.fadeIn();
			window.setInterval(function(){var _this = jQuery('#optin_link_process_dots' + link_id);var num = _this.data('num');if(typeof(num)=='undefined'){num=0;}var dots='';for(var i =0;i<num;i++){dots+='.';}_this.text(dots);var dir = _this.data('dir');if(typeof(dir)=='undefined'){dir=1;}if(num > 3){dir = -1;}if(num < 0){dir = 1;}num += dir; _this.data('num',num); _this.data('dir',dir);},250);
			var data = {'dataType' : 'json',
							'data': {'action' : 'opt_create_lead',
									'visitor_cookie' : dwpc_visitor_id,
									'impression_id' : dwpc_impression_id,
									'forms_id' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('form_id'),
									'links_id' : link_id,
									'link_tracking_id' : $opt_cur_form_container.data('opt_link_tracking_id'),
									'email' : $email.val(),
									'name' : $name.val(),
									'secured_page' : opt_secured_page_id,
									'no_thanks' : 1 },
						'success' : function(data,textStatus,jqXHR){
							$opt_cur_form_container.data('clicked',false);
							if(opt_ajax_options(data)){return;}
							
							$form.hide();
							$form_success.show();
							
							opt_redir_url = data['redir_url'];
							
							opt_set_cookie(data);
							
							
							window.setTimeout(function(){
								window.location = opt_redir_url;
							},3*1000);
						}};
			
			jQuery.ajax(opt_ajaxurl, data);	
			
		}
	}
	function opt_find_value(id){
		if(typeof(id) != 'string'){return '';}
		
		var $obj = jQuery('#'+id);
		if($obj.length == 0){return '';}
		
		return $obj.val();
			
	}
	function opt_element_exists(id){
		if(typeof(id) != 'string'){return false;}
		
		var $obj = jQuery('#'+id);
		if($obj.length == 0){return false;}
		return true;	
	}
	function opt_check_elem(id){
		var find_value = opt_find_value(id)!='';
		var elem_exists = opt_element_exists(id);
		return !elem_exists || (elem_exists && find_value);	
	}
	function opt_rgxemvd(inp){return /[^\s@]+@[^\s@]+\.[^\s@]+/.test(inp);}
	function rawurlencode(str) { str = (str + '').toString();return encodeURIComponent(str).replace(/!/g, '%21').replace(/'/g, '%27').replace(/\(/g, '%28').replace(/\)/g, '%29').replace(/\*/g, '%2A').replace(/~/g, '%7E');}

				<article id="post-17427" class="et_pb_post post-17427 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-blogging-social-media tag-alexa-rank tag-blog-traffic tag-conversations tag-engagement tag-entrepreneur tag-page-rank tag-page-views">
											<div class="et_post_meta_wrapper">
							<h1 class="entry-title">Every Entrepreneur That Blogs Regrets Not Doing This Sooner</h1>

						<p class="post-meta"> by <span class="author vcard"><a href="http://www.adriennesmith.net/author/enosihtsseugrevenlliwuoy/" title="Posts by Adrienne Smith" rel="author">Adrienne Smith</a></span> | <span class="published">Feb 8, 2016</span> | <span class="comments-number"><a href="http://www.adriennesmith.net/entrepreneur-blogs-regrets-this/#respond">98 comments</a></span></p>
												</div> <!-- .et_post_meta_wrapper -->
				
					<div class="entry-content">
					<p><img class="alignleft size-full wp-image-17435" src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/EntrepreneurRegretC.jpg" alt="Entrepreneur Blogs Regret Not Doing" width="640" height="463" srcset="http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/EntrepreneurRegretC-400x289.jpg 400w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/EntrepreneurRegretC-610x441.jpg 610w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/EntrepreneurRegretC.jpg 640w" sizes="(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px" />As the years progress and time goes by, how many things have you seen drastically change since you started blogging?</p>
<p>Most know my history already, that I started doing affiliate marketing and like most people taught back around 2008, it was ALL about backlinks and keywords.</p>
<p>Why?</p>
<p>Because it just worked that’s why.</p>
<p>It worked because people were online searching for something and the more backlinks you had pointing to your blog and the more keywords you had stuffed in your content the easier you were found in the search engines.</p>
<p>Of course it was all about selling products and people were much more open to buying.</p>
<p>Then the black hat marketers got involved and wanted to make the quick buck.  They wanted to outdo everyone else and make sure their content was found much quicker and they didn’t want to take the time to build things up.</p>
<p>So Google got smart, changed the algorithms once again and those days of easily being found were gone.</p>
<p>Want to know what else is gone?</p>
<p>Numbers….</p>
<h2><span style="font-family: 'All Things Pink'; color: #071331;">Change Is Inevitable</span></h2>
<p>Oftentimes I’ll receive an email from someone who is panicked and desperate.</p>
<p>It breaks my heart actually because I know how they feel.</p>
<p>We come online, we follow certain people, we’re taught certain things and they guarantee us that it will work.</p>
<p>Well not every single thing works for every single person.  I think that’s the case only because we’re all different and unique in our own ways.</p>
<p>That doesn’t necessarily mean that what they teach doesn’t work, it just might not work for you.  But there are those people unfortunately that are still teaching things that haven’t worked in YEARS…</p>
<p>Beth is a budding entrepreneur who was upset because she was still being taught that she had to drive tons of traffic to her blog.  Okay well we do need traffic because without eyeballs on our content then there will be no people to take that next step right!</p>
<p>Unfortunately for Beth, she was still being taught to just drive traffic to her blog without concentrating on targeted traffic.  She was still being taught that it was all about the numbers.</p>
<p>It’s not about the numbers anymore, it’s not about just anyone seeing your content, it’s about only driving targeted traffic to your blog.  Those people who are interested in what it is that you’re offering.</p>
<p>Granted there are so many other things that have to be in place as well <a href="http://www.adriennesmith.net/how-to-write-content-guarantee-results/" target="_blank">like your message and your content</a> but what I want to bring to your attention in this post is that <span style="color: #071331;"><strong>the way things are progressing</strong></span> is that it’s more about <span style="color: #071331;"><strong>what you do with those people</strong></span> once they are on your blog.</p>

		<div class="sw-tweet-clear"></div>
		<a class="sw_CTT style1" href="https://twitter.com/share?text=Don%27t+be+afraid+of+change.+It%27s+leading+you+to+a+new+beginning.&url=http://www.adriennesmith.net/entrepreneur-blogs-regrets-this/%3Futm_source%3Dtwitter%26utm_medium%3Dsocial%26utm_campaign%3DSocialWarfare&via=adriennesmith40" data-link="https://twitter.com/share?text=Don%27t+be+afraid+of+change.+It%27s+leading+you+to+a+new+beginning.&url=http://www.adriennesmith.net/entrepreneur-blogs-regrets-this/%3Futm_source%3Dtwitter%26utm_medium%3Dsocial%26utm_campaign%3DSocialWarfare&via=adriennesmith40" target="_blank"><span class="sw-click-to-tweet"><span class="sw-ctt-text">Don't be afraid of change. It's leading you to a new beginning.</span><span class="sw-ctt-btn">Click To Tweet<i class="sw sw-twitter"></i></span></span></a>
<h2><span style="font-family: 'All Things Pink'; color: #071331;">Unique Visitors and Page Views</span></h2>
<p>Do you remember the days when what mattered the most was your Page Rank, how many unique visitors you had coming to your blog and how many page views you were getting?</p>
<p>How about your Alexa Rank?  If it was really low then people just assumed that you were very successful.  Possibly someone extremely important.</p>
<p>Did having great numbers in all of those area mean instant success?</p>
<p>Absolutely not!</p>
<p><img class="aligncenter wp-image-17450" src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC.jpg" alt="Just Numbers" width="928" height="396" srcset="http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC-400x171.jpg 400w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC-768x328.jpg 768w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC-1024x437.jpg 1024w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC-610x260.jpg 610w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC-1080x461.jpg 1080w, http://www.adriennesmith.net/adriennesmith/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/JustNumbersC.jpg 1279w" sizes="(max-width: 928px) 100vw, 928px" /></p>
<p>It’s probably been a good four years since I had a PR4 blog and it’s been two years since my Alexa Rank was around 24,000.</p>
<p>To someone who doesn’t know any better they would have instantly thought I was successful.</p>
<p>Guess what!</p>
<p>I wasn’t, not back then…</p>
<p>I’ve had a PR2 for about three years now and since I only post once a week my Alexa Rank keeps climbing.  The funny thing though is that I’m more successful now then I was back then.</p>
<p>Want to know why?</p>
<p>It’s the engagement that matters the most, not the amount of traffic that you get.</p>
<p>I know what you’re thinking though. I’ve always had a lot of engagement here on my blog.</p>
<p>My issue was <span style="color: #071331;"><strong>what I did with that engagement</strong></span>.  I didn’t quite have everything together several years ago but I finally fell into what I enjoyed doing the most and it’s just expanded from there.</p>
<p>That’s the issue Beth was also seeing.  The traffic was great but it wasn’t targeted.  Her message was clear but her content wasn’t speaking to her specific audience.</p>
<p>She definitely wasn’t having the engagement that she needed so we’re working together now to get her on the right track.  Of course since she is working with me now that gives her instant access to my <a href="http://buildblogcommunity.com/" target="_blank">Build a Blog Community course</a>.</p>
<h2><span style="font-family: 'All Things Pink'; color: #071331;">Engagement Is What Closes Deals</span></h2>
<p>Predictions have been made for this year as well on this topic, surprise!</p>
<p>We all need traffic to our blogs that’s a given.</p>
<p>Page views are important so we can gauge what they’re viewing the most.</p>
<p>Can you attract the reader though and keep them on your site?  Can you get them engaged, can you <a href="http://buildblogcommunity.com/" target="_blank">create a community</a> that will keep them coming back time and time again because of what you offer?</p>
<p>Once you hit publish do you have loyal readers showing up, reading your content and then sharing it on social media?  Do you have them telling their friends about you?</p>
<p>Are you engaging with them enough so that those that do want what you have to offer will buy from you?</p>
<p>I watched a <a href="http://blog.eonetwork.org/2016/01/jasons-2016-prediction-converting-online-traffic-to-increased-sales/" target="_blank">very interesting video</a> from Jason Forrest who is the CEO of Forrest Performance Group.  In this video he did make his own predictions about this area as well.</p>
<p>He is referencing sites like Twitter but blogging is also a part of social media.  His point is that when someone says something about your content, don’t just say “oh thanks, glad you liked it”.  Interact with them, get engaged with that person and <span style="color: #071331;"><strong>make a connection</strong></span>.</p>
<p>Schedule a phone conversation with them or for me I love Skype because you can do face to face.</p>
<p>That’s the way you close deals, get sales, work with people.  Comments are great but that’s the beginning of the conversation so you better be having some great conversations on your blog and/or through email.</p>
<p>You wouldn’t believe the amount of emails that I get from people who have been reading my content yet have never left a comment.  They have resonated with what I’ve shared and email me when they’re ready to have that <a href="http://www.adriennesmith.net/free-consultation/" target="_blank">free 30 minute consultation</a>.</p>
<p>We go over what they’re struggling with the most and then they&#8217;re ready to get to work.  It’s a beautiful thing.</p>
<p>Take it a step further is what I’m saying.</p>
<p>We don’t need someone predicting how important this is, it’s always been important.</p>
<p>Numbers are great but they’re just numbers unless you’re getting results.  We all want traffic, readers, comments and shares.  That’s a big part of us building up an authority online in the area that we’re devoted to.</p>
<p>You have to get those conversations started though, get people engaged on your blog and then have those discussions with them that can lead to potential clients and/or sales.</p>
<p>Not everyone will buy from you but through those relationships you’re building they’ll recommend people to you which to me is the best type of traffic.</p>

		<div class="sw-tweet-clear"></div>
		<a class="sw_CTT style1" href="https://twitter.com/share?text=%27Most+are+all+about+the+number%27s%2C+you+should+be+all+about+the+relationships%21%27+%7E+Adrienne+Smith&url=http://www.adriennesmith.net/entrepreneur-blogs-regrets-this/%3Futm_source%3Dtwitter%26utm_medium%3Dsocial%26utm_campaign%3DSocialWarfare&via=adriennesmith40" data-link="https://twitter.com/share?text=%27Most+are+all+about+the+number%27s%2C+you+should+be+all+about+the+relationships%21%27+%7E+Adrienne+Smith&url=http://www.adriennesmith.net/entrepreneur-blogs-regrets-this/%3Futm_source%3Dtwitter%26utm_medium%3Dsocial%26utm_campaign%3DSocialWarfare&via=adriennesmith40" target="_blank"><span class="sw-click-to-tweet"><span class="sw-ctt-text">'Most are all about the number's, you should be all about the relationships!' ~ Adrienne Smith</span><span class="sw-ctt-btn">Click To Tweet<i class="sw sw-twitter"></i></span></span></a>
<h2><span style="font-family: 'All Things Pink'; color: #071331;">Success Is Yours This Year</span></h2>
<p>Beth has been having some aha moments.  I get that a lot when I work with my clients.</p>
<p>Blogging is the marketing tool you should be using to get your target audience interested in what you offer.</p>
<p>It should have them saying you were speaking just to me or how did he/she know that’s what I was thinking.</p>
<p>It should relate to what their problem is at that moment and then get them engaged in the comment section so you can open up that conversation.  They don&#8217;t even really have to comment though, they can send you an email.</p>
<p>Your next step should be to have that personal conversation with them so you can find out what their issues, needs or problem is.  I know everyone is different but you can’t go wrong having that one-on-one conversation with someone.</p>
<p>Success is yours this year so no matter what changes continue to happen as the years go by, you’ve got to have everything in place so that they&#8217;re eager to take that next step with you.</p>
<p>Numbers are impressive but they don’t close sales.  Get them engaged and if you haven’t been doing this up to this point then you better start today.</p>
<p>Stop struggling in this area and let’s devise a plan of action.  I offer a 30 minute free consultation so <a href="http://www.adriennesmith.net/free-consultation/" target="_blank">click this link now</a> and let’s get you headed for success.</p>

				<p>What an awesome post, Adrienne!</p>
<p>It&#8217;s like you read my mind!</p>
<p>The topic of the rant video I&#8217;m publishing tomorrow is &#8220;Forget about the Numbers.&#8221;</p>
<p>Too many marketers and bloggers focused only on how many Instagram followers they have have, how many people on their mailing list, how many hits their blog gets each month&#8230;</p>
<p>And while we all want to have a large following, its importance pales in comparison to real, active, engaged, human followers&#8230; the people who actually give a sh*t about what we have to say!</p>
<p>I&#8217;d rather have 1,000 followers who care about my message than 10,000 followers who ignore me.</p>
<p>Or, as Don Purdum says, people who are ready, willing, and able to buy from us.</p>

				<p>Hey Brent,</p>
<p>Great to see you again my friend!</p>
<p>Well I guess as we move into this year and see what&#8217;s important and what really isn&#8217;t then maybe more people will be sharing their views about this topic.  I&#8217;m tired of hearing people teach others how to drive traffic and that it&#8217;s just a numbers game.  All I can say is good luck with that.</p>

Not that theirs don&#8217;t so let me rephrase that because we each know what our business is doing behind closed doors.  My following is loyal and active and they take action.  </p>

	<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-66662">
		<article id="comment-66662" class="comment-body clearfix">
			<div class="comment_avatar">
				<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f9faeb5e1e5ee4ae9aff03212a629188?s=80&#038;d=monsterid&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f9faeb5e1e5ee4ae9aff03212a629188?s=160&amp;d=monsterid&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-80 photo' height='80' width='80' />			</div>

			<div class="comment_postinfo">
				<span class="fn">Ben</span>				<span class="comment_date">
				on February 13, 2016 at 10:28 AM				</span>
										</div> <!-- .comment_postinfo -->

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne. I agree with a lot of what you said. When I originally started blogging several years ago I followed a lot of the big name blogging &#8220;gurus&#8221; and everything I was taught was about the numbers, all of the stats that Google Analytics can give you. Even back then though, Google said that it was about the content, about writing for a real person to read. I think engagement naturally grows out of content. To create good content you have to have an idea of what your audience wants to read. Google has done their best to root out the tricks that people used to boost the numbers and when they couldn&#8217;t, they reduced the importance of the numbers. I have worked with a few people over the years who spent so much time obsessing about the numbers that they never actually did anything to change the numbers. Now Google has figured out ways to measure engagement so they have included them in their algorithm and further reduced the importance of the numbers. The numbers are still there behind the engagement, so they are still important but Google doesn&#8217;t have to measure them directly anymore. The basics of writing to a real person have always mattered, and still do. I think it&#8217;s another case of &#8220;the more things change, the more they stay the same.&#8221; Just my 2 cents.</p>

				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>For someone whose numbers aren&#8217;t amazing (me) that&#8217;s one very encouraging post!</p>
<p>If it were all about the numbers I would have given up long ago &#8211; but thankfully I met some really great bloggers who taught me otherwise. Probably you were one of the first of them, but someone must have sent me to you. I think it was Angela&#8230;. I certainly owe her a debt of gratitude, because it was that &#8220;introduction&#8221; that was the turning point for me.</p>
<p>I don&#8217;t bother much thinking about keywords and SEO any more, because the number of sites I&#8217;d have to try and beat are just so silly. I just blog about what&#8217;s been happening to me over the week and that&#8217;s never let me down for a topic &#8211; and happily people I&#8217;ve met though nice bloggers like yourself seem to come along and join in.</p>
<p>Such a far cry from one of my earlier &#8220;decent&#8221; blogs (I scrapped a few rubbish ones first!) when &#8211; although I was working really hard on creating well-research posts in the health niche (three times a week), NO-ONE was coming. That was so depressing. That&#8217;s over. I scrapped that blog too, which was a shame because tons of work had gone into it, but never mind. I actually like my current one better, so I hope it reflects that in my posts.</p>
<p>Oops &#8211; better &#8220;do something&#8221;, I&#8217;m getting carried away chatting!</p>
<p>Have a good weekend,  Joy<br />

				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne<br />
Talking makes the world go round. Throw smiling and sharing into the mix and you have a winning recipe. Touch emotions and you have listener. Offer your listener help and encouragement and you have a friend.</p>
<p>Blogging can be such a powerful tool. Speak to people not to numbers. Talk about them and not about what you sell. People do not read newspapers to read the ads. They read the news because news stirs emotions. That is the way you should blog.</p>
<p>Internet marketing teachers often say you should give value. Everyone has a story to tell but often he or she has nobody to tell it to. Be an open ear, a shoulder to cry on and a helping hand at the same time. That is the best kind of value there is.</p>
<p>Thanks for pointing out how to engage your readers and why you should do so. </p>
<p>Great post.<br />
Igert</p>

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>Where some get it wrong is taking the internet business as the business of the robot; no&#8230;..it doesn&#8217;t have to be seen that way.</p>
<p>Internet business is a people&#8217;s business and unless you treat it as such, you might not get too far with it.</p>
<p>Whatever it takes to do business successfully in the offline world also apply here, you&#8217;ll need to talk to people, get to know them and make them trust you.</p>
<p>If people don&#8217;t trust you, they won&#8217;t buy from you. And how do you get all these things in a faceless community like the internet?</p>
<p>You start by engaging in meaningful discussions with genuine and relevant audience.</p>
<p>I have had few discussions online with people I never before from Adam that had resulted into paying blog coaching sessions over the years.</p>
<p>Attending live industry event is what I like mention here too, it helps a lot in meeting relevant people and establishing new connections.</p>
<p>I have maintain few connections from years of attending such events that are still helpful till date.</p>
<p>It dosen&#8217;t have to stop on our blog, we can take it further to real life and open dooors for new opportunities.</p>
<p>Thanks Adrienne, nice read.<br />

				<p>Hey Peter,</p>
<p>Well I always love hearing that Peter.</p>
<p>I believe that&#8217;s what people need to do more of.  I had a girl reach out to me and we had a terrific Skype chat yesterday as well.  We&#8217;ve known who each other is online for years now, commented a few times on each other&#8217;s blog but never made that connection.  I&#8217;m SO glad we did too because I got a LOT out of our conversation just like you and I did last week as well.  It just helps people be more connected and that&#8217;s where friendships can be formed and you and I both know, referrals can come from.  Not everyone is our client or customer but they know someone who is.  😉</p>
<p>You&#8217;re really great at helping people Peter and you connect really well with others.  Just think of that person who follows you on Twitter, what it would mean to them for you to reach out and ask if there is anything you can help them with at this moment.  Or they share your content and you start a conversation with them besides just thanking them for sharing it.  People aren&#8217;t doing that, they all have an agenda but you never know where that will lead unless you make that next step.</p>
<p>It&#8217;s been mind boggling the people who email me who have never commented on my blog.  Some are on my list yet have never communicated with me before.  I love it though because they&#8217;re listening and paying attention.  You just never know who you&#8217;ll reach.</p>
<p>This is why you need to continue speaking to that one person who has that one problem Peter.  It&#8217;s going to resonate with your audience, they&#8217;re going to have those aha moments, they&#8217;re going to eventually reach out to you when they&#8217;re ready because they need to make sure you&#8217;re the one that can really help them.  Just know that they&#8217;re watching you.</p>
<p>Thank you Peter for the comment, you know I always appreciate it.  You have a great end to your week okay!</p>

				<p>Hey Vee and Ric,</p>
<p>What you have to remember my friend is that Google is here to make money, plain and simple.  They are also a search engine but that means it&#8217;s just a program that they keep working on in order to find the best content possible for whatever the person is searching for.  Personally, I feel they&#8217;ve gotten much better because when I used to search for stuff I got way too much junk.  Today I get a lot of great content that I was searching for but for you to rank on the first page of Google, well you&#8217;ve got to put your work in just like everyone else.</p>
<p>Don&#8217;t count on Google though, you can&#8217;t just rely on one source of traffic so go out there, make your own traffic and over time Google will notice.  You need to start making those connections though with the people who show up on your site.  It will happen in time when you do this process right.</p>
<p>I wish you the best as always so have fun with this okay!</p>

<p>Wonderful to see you again, thanks for dropping by.</p>
<p>That&#8217;s what it should be about because if you&#8217;re blogging to build your business then you need to make the connections with those interested in what it is that you offer.  Numbers can be good for different reasons but if people keep banking on it as a guaranteed success then they&#8217;re going to be in for a rude awakening.  </p>
<p>SEO will always be alive, it&#8217;s how we use it that continues to change but I think for the most part the way it is right now is the way it will stay.  I mean using SEO is more natural for me and has been for several years now and it still works beautifully.  We definitely shouldn&#8217;t obsess over it though because you&#8217;re right, we never know what Google will do next.</p>
<p>I love talking with people and helping them.  It&#8217;s just what I enjoy the most so if I can combine that with them purchasing from me, those that need it, then that&#8217;s just an added bonus for me.</p>
<p>I appreciate your visit and comment today Katrin.  Thank you so much and you have a terrific rest of your week okay!</p>
<p>~Adrienne</p>

				<p>Hey Adrienne,</p>
<p>A couple of years ago, I came to the realization that statistics are great motivation factors, but it doesn&#8217;t mean that you&#8217;re successful.</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve seen a couple of bloggers who went from have just over 1,000 on their alexa and now they have over 1 million alexa score. You and me know what happened with this. At the time, judging from their stats, I thought they were successful, but apparently not.</p>
<p>As you&#8217;ve said, the key is engaging. You want to engage with those that share a common interest and common goals as you do. When people can resonate well with you, then that&#8217;s when growing your blog and home business becomes less of a challenge. We all need traffic to come to our blog, but the real question when it comes down to it is what type of traffic do we need.</p>

			<div class="comment_avatar">
				<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/18a24e167143e3305e08c3700ed81370?s=80&#038;d=monsterid&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/18a24e167143e3305e08c3700ed81370?s=160&amp;d=monsterid&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-80 photo' height='80' width='80' />			</div>

			<div class="comment_postinfo">
				<span class="fn"><a href='http://trafficsmartmarketing.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Tom Southern</a><br />Twitter: <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" class="twitter-anywhere-user" href="http://twitter.com/CopyByTom">CopyByTom</a><br /></span>				<span class="comment_date">

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>This post really resonates for me at the moment.</p>
<p>I too have had some landmark moments recently. Just in the last 7 days, I&#8217;ve had an email from one reader who is really struggling to find a niche and is chasing his tail trying to pinpoint<br />
what his niche actually is. He can&#8217;t get to grips with the concept that it&#8217;s not about finding<br />
keywords and continually getting traffic.</p>
<p>Another reader opened up to me about how they&#8217;re a complete beginner and finding all the advice  out there overwhelming.</p>
<p>To both, I&#8217;ve been telling them that success is all about relationships and engagement is a big part of this. </p>
<p>But, in the beginning, I say to people struggling, that it&#8217;s about finding the right traffic for your blog. Simply, the right traffic consists of people like you. People who are going through what you went through to get to where you are now. To them, you&#8217;re an authority because you know what steps to take to get to where you are.</p>
<p>But you need to let them know that you can help them get to where you are. You do this by making  a connection, engaging, showing them you&#8217;re open to more of their questions, you&#8217;ll willing to respond to them when they tweet you, or email you, or leave comments. </p>
<p>I always try to leave any communication I have with people with a question about them, if it&#8217;s<br />
appropriate. This almost always gets them to respond, thus opening the door to real communication.</p>
<p>The more real your communication the more likely you are to attract the right kind of traffic to  your blog and start making it work successfully for you.</p>
<p>Btw, do you record your Skype consultations and, if so, how do you record them?</p>
<p>&#8211; Tom<br />
<span class="cluv">Tom Southern recently posted&#8230;<a class="45226e25b4 66614" rel="external" href="http://trafficsmartmarketing.com/still-struggling-to-find-your-niche-heres-why/">STILL STRUGGLING TO FIND YOUR NICHE? HERE’S WHY…</a><span class="heart_tip_box"><img class="heart_tip u 66614 24e16" alt="My Profile" style="border:0" width="16" height="14" src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/wp-content/plugins/commentluv-premium/images/littleheart.gif"/></span></span></p>

<p>Another week, another a-ha moment from you (not that I am the first to say that).</p>
<p>When you talk about numbers vs relationships, it reminds me of the scenario where someone has an address book or business card holder that is bulging with contacts. They are very proud of just how many &#8216;contacts&#8217; they have but how many of those do they actually interact with on a regular basis or even know very well?</p>
<p>Not many I would bet.</p>
<p>And that is the point isn&#8217;t it. It isn&#8217;t about how many contacts we have. It is the quality of those contacts. The people we take the time to build relationships with. Our loyal fans that we would recommend and who would recommend us.</p>
<p>Definitely something to always remember.</p>

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne</p>
<p>A-ha moments.  I live for those!  My theory is that forward movement is dependent on how many aha moments we have in a given time frame.</p>
<p>Last year I had many of those individual moments, which in turn facilitated a massive shift in the way I was doing business.  Previously I was running ads, calling leads and (hopefully) making sales.</p>
<p>Now it&#8217;s all organic.  It&#8217;s about engagement, warmth, friendships, value giving, and sharing.  What an enormous change this has been.  Although my income dropped a lot, the vital signs are looking good.  I made the change because I wanted a more sustainable income stream, and a more enriching working experience.  </p>
<p>For people reading this &#8211; especially newbies &#8211; I say this to you:  play the long game.  This is not a sprint; it&#8217;s a marathon for sure.  Is it worth it?  Well, yes.  Creating long term sustainable income is always worth the effort.  So be patient, and take the focus away from making money for a while and just focus on audience and relationship building for now.</p>
<p>You talk about taking engagement further.  I agree, and not just on our blog.  An example: in the last week I&#8217;ve had several appointments (via Skype) from people who reached out to me.  They didn&#8217;t come from my blog but Facebook.  I had been engaging with them for a little while, and when the timing was right, they reached out.  (One little technique I am using now is to use the FB chat facility to thank people for liking my post &#8211; sometimes a valuable conversation can flow from this simple activity.)</p>
<p>So yeah this stuff is working, and I can thank Ryan Biddulph for being the original catalyst.  He was the change agent I needed at that time simply because I was ready.  Since then I&#8217;ve met wonderful people like yourself who have helped me refine what I was doing and move to the next level.</p>
<p>I urge readers to get hold of your Build a Blog Community Course or book a consultation, a game changer, no doubt. </p>
<p>Cheers</p>
<p>Kim<br />

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Adrienne, I totally agree with this post. So many bloggers focus on the numbers when they don&#8217;t mean all that much. I myself am guilty of sneaking off during dinner to check my WordPress stats. </p>
<p>However, I have experienced first hand that, as you wrote, you don&#8217;t need hundreds of thousands of page views a month to be successful. You need to know what your superpowers are, who your ideal audience members are, and then engage with them in a way that&#8217;s unique to you.</p>
<p>The other thing about numbers is that they aren&#8217;t there to support you in your blogging journey. They won&#8217;t give you feedback on your posts and they won&#8217;t send you messages that let you know, without a doubt, that your voice matters. Only people and relationships can do that!</p>

	<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="li-comment-66597">
		<article id="comment-66597" class="comment-body clearfix">
			<div class="comment_avatar">
				<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0884cc01c74b427e2f5fe8b6b8e3d790?s=80&#038;d=monsterid&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0884cc01c74b427e2f5fe8b6b8e3d790?s=160&amp;d=monsterid&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-80 photo' height='80' width='80' />			</div>

			<div class="comment_postinfo">
				<span class="fn"><a href='http://HelpStartMySite.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>James McAllister</a><br />Twitter: <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" class="twitter-anywhere-user" href="http://twitter.com/HelpStartMySite">HelpStartMySite</a><br /></span>				<span class="comment_date">
				on February 8, 2016 at 7:04 PM				</span>
										</div> <!-- .comment_postinfo -->

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne!</p>
<p>Seems like so many people, especially beginners forget that the basic rules of sales determine a lot of their success. Every blogger is a salesperson, even if they are just trying to sell their ideas. People tend to forget that. </p>
<p>With my first blog I blogged as the brand rather than a person – people didn’t really have any idea who I actually was or what I was like. This made it hard to connect with them, and as a result few people trusted me enough to make any meaningful purchases through that site. No doubt if I were selling my own products (I was only an affiliate at that time) my sales would have been even lower. </p>
<p>The problem with many of our blogs, especially those of us working in the hobby type niches, is that people don’t wake up one day and decide they want to buy a similar type of product we’re trying to sell them. Instead, we need to connect with them and sell them on the value of the product. We can’t just sit back and wait for that to happen, we need to engage with them so they can see it, and trust us enough to buy it. Otherwise, another marketer who does go after it will win their sale. </p>
<p>Big numbers are great but like you said without results they’re just numbers. My first blog that did decent had thousands of visitors a day at one point but I didn’t know how to monetize. Without a system in place to really connect with those visitors, more traffic doesn’t help us all that much. </p>
<p>Success with engagement perpetuates success through referrals as you mentioned so no doubt this is the way to go.</p>
<p>Thanks Adrienne!<br />
<span class="cluv">James McAllister recently posted&#8230;<a class="921547362f 66597 p" rel="nofollow" href="http://helpstartmysite.com/bloggers-purpose-reasons-social-media/">Most Bloggers Are Using Social Media For The Wrong Reasons</a><span class="heart_tip_box"><img class="heart_tip p 66597 4cc01" alt="My Profile" style="border:0" width="16" height="14" src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/wp-content/plugins/commentluv-premium/images/littleheartplus.gif"/></span></span></p>

				<p>Hey James,</p>
<p>I know for me when I first started I was insulted if someone called me a salesperson.  I grew up though with a Dad who was in sales and he used to critique every sales guy we ever crossed and trust me, 98% of them failed miserably so it was almost like saying a dirty word to me.  It wasn&#8217;t until much later that I came to the realization that I&#8217;m selling myself although I&#8217;m nowhere near like those creepy sales guys I always ran into.  I&#8217;m sure I&#8217;m not the only one who thought that way either.</p>
<p>Thanks for sharing with me the experiences you&#8217;ve had.  I can relate to the brand because I was doing affiliate marketing as well but it was all about the product and I didn&#8217;t really share anything about me.  It worked up to a point until everything changed then it just all feel apart.</p>
<p>I can understand what you&#8217;re saying about hobby niches.  I&#8217;m sure though that even with different types of hobbies that they are searching for certain things although not all.  But you&#8217;re right, striking up those conversations and learning more about them definitely will benefit you much greater then just sitting back and waiting for them to hopefully find you.  By that time someone else has definitely snatched them up already.</p>
<p>We definitely need to have something in place to close the deals and make those sales.  Without that we&#8217;ll all just be blogging as a hobby.</p>
<p>Thanks James for your comment and you be sure to have a great week okay!</p>

				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>In all honesty, I would be turned off to blogging if it was still just about the numbers.</p>
<p>In fact, the reason I fell in love with having a blog is because of the relationships.<br />
I prefer to work with what I am passionate about. Those who come to my blog engage with me. I&#8217;ve had so many people open up and share personal experiences in the comment&#8217;s section (and in guest posts) that it has established a beautiful level of trust and community. </p>
<p>I wasn&#8217;t surprised when things had changed several years ago with Google and their algorithms. People were building these websites without an actual human connection behind the efforts. Things become sloppy and there are consequences. The only real way to do any sort of business is to be fully present. </p>
<p>It&#8217;s really the only way to live in general.</p>
<p>If it weren&#8217;t for the community aspect of building a blog that speaks to real humans who want to hear from YOU, this could be a lonely and frustrating endeavor.</p>
<p>We all support one another (and do business with one another) based on that level of trust that only happens when we feel we&#8217;ve been heard, understood and cared about.</p>
<p>I&#8217;m not surprised your business is booming. It should be <img src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /><br />

It&#8217;s not just about reading content, buying and moving on anymore.  Not what I&#8217;ve witnessed at least.</p>

Most people though have questions and run into issues with any type of product so knowing someone is behind it definitely helps.</p>

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>It&#8217;s so weird. How folks obsess about numbers over bonds. All that black hat stuff and focus on outcomes seems to be dying, slowly but surely, as your message is ringing loud and clear. More bloggers are onboard with making friends with niche-specific folks and with publish niche-specific posts for their audiences, and are moving away from the outcomes-driven stuff which has led to much blogging failure.</p>
<p>Numbers do not buy courses or eBooks. Numbers can&#8217;t read posts or RT posts or comment on posts. Numbers can&#8217;t grow blogs or join lists. Yet many folks are hellbent on getting big numbers in traffic and list terms. It&#8217;s silly. And your post shows how the quality of your bonds surely points you in the right blogging direction.</p>
<p>I love having fun with my blog. Because when I post from a fun, more-detached space, I stay on topic, I comment on relevant blogs and I watch my presence expand without wheel spinning ways. The struggling bit is rooted in moving away from having fun with creating and making friends (the powerful, light, relaxed stuff) towards tension&#8230;.tension based in giving your energy to numbers and other imaginary things. Have fun creating posts for people. Have fun connecting with people. Don&#8217;t build tension in your body by trying to establish a bond with things. Things can&#8217;t love you back. People can. And will. When you give them your attention, when you help and promote them and when you connect with them thru commenting and social media and email.</p>
<p>Numbers can&#8217;t grow your blog. Honest. I tried it. Tried forming bonds with numbers by obsessing over them. The moment I dropped the tension-filled, numbers focused energy it&#8217;s like I sent out a loud and clear signal to folks who dug my blog: I am here, to help, to energize and to connect with you. What a night day difference in this approach.</p>
<p>Have a fabulous week Adrienne.</p>
<p>Ryan<br />

				<p>Happy Birthday Ryan!</p>
<p>That&#8217;s the direction that has always worked in the past and I guess some people are hell bent on letting that go.  I can&#8217;t for the life of me though think that still works for them.  We all know that it&#8217;s the follow through that counts and not just the numbers.</p>
<p>We need our readers to take action and only when they do can we follow up with them.  Only when they do can we open that conversation and help them further.  That&#8217;s what gets them interested enough to either keep on coming back or wanting to buy from us.</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve been following a particular lady online Ryan who teaches about the law of attraction.  She teaches it in a way though that most don&#8217;t and I guess that&#8217;s what I happen to love about her.  It works because she&#8217;s been living it for the past 40 some odd years.  She basically says the same thing, just have fun with it.  Stop obsessing over everything and put it out to the Universe what you want and then just get to work.  Everything will fall into place as it should and she&#8217;s right.  I&#8217;ve already in such a short time seen just that happen.  </p>
<p>I&#8217;m glad you dropped the numbers game too.  I never really obsessed over that myself although I will say that I thought about it.  I&#8217;m glad though that I didn&#8217;t take that particular stance and look at me now!  😉  Look at you now!  Got to love it right!</p>

				<p>Hi Adrienne</p>
<p>First of all I highly appreciate your consistently firm resolve to help your readers that is reflected in your each post where you very generously offer your one-on-one counselling to those who are still confused how to do successful blogging in this era of dog-eats-dog competition.</p>
<p>I remember quite vividly of my first content writing order that I got with a clear instruction how many times I must use a keyword in a 500-word post and how smartly I should equally use related keywords several times as well.</p>
<p>But later on all of a sudden many things changed a lot and this was because of frequent Google updates that replaced the numbers with quality and most of the rules of offline publishing equally applied in online publishing. Since then it is quality that leads the rest of the criteria and that is why survivors are those now who are genuine and firmly believe in true professionalism. </p>
<p>Many thanks for sharing yet another post of high value fully packed with your worthwhile experience of blogging as well as of corporate America. </p>
<p>Have a great rest of the week.<br />

				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>How are you today? I see you&#8217;re off to a good start this week. <img src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /> </p>
<p>Numbers are cold data. They&#8217;re important for sure. Traffic numbers give bloggers feedback on visits per month, unique visits, which is part of the equation. </p>
<p>Those cold numbers stay cold though if we are do not have a warm heart and build relationships. </p>
<p>Those numbers don&#8217;t convert if we are only focused on traffic. </p>
<p>Numbers are fickle and can rise and fall by the thousands from month to month. If you confidence is married to those cold numbers, you will have a nervous breakdown. </p>
<p>You lead by example here. You engage, build relationships, support others. Respond quickly. Keep your word. Build trust&#8230;the things we all need to do with those cold numbers to make them useful. </p>
<p>This is a timely reminder and I&#8217;ll be sharing this, Adrienne.<br />
Have an awesome week, my friend. </p>
<p>Keep shining,</p>
<p>Matthew</p>

				on February 8, 2016 at 10:07 AM				</span>

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hey Adrienne,</p>
<p>Google sure has changed A LOT these last few years. </p>
<p>It&#8217;s so sad when some of those so called gooroo&#8217;s (yep, I spelled that wrong) keep on teaching things that aren&#8217;t effective anymore. It seems like they don&#8217;t want to guide people, they&#8217;re just out for the quick buck. </p>
<p>Saying you have to get &#8220;traffic&#8221; is obviously way too abstract. Obviously, more eyeballs are more chances to make a sale, but targeted traffic is key. You&#8217;re so right.  </p>
<p>I think Jason&#8217;s view is interesting. I hope there&#8217;s going to be a middle road. I believe that people have taken more power now because of social media, and if companies start viewing every single social interaction turns into a conversion opportunity, people will respond accordingly. </p>
<p>I think this is where Gary&#8217;s jab, jab, jab, right hook philosophy comes from and why he says &#8220;marketers ruin everything&#8221;. </p>
<p>However, I totally agree with your view that instead of saying &#8220;thanks for sharing&#8221; (we might as well use automated tools then, right?) we could use those opportunities to create meaningful connections which will eventually turn into more sales.</p>
<p>Of course, I&#8217;m not surprised that Beth had her share of aha moments after working with you. You&#8217;re just a fantastic coach and you know how to help others break through their most important issues. </p>
<p>This was an awesome post and quite inspirational, too. I&#8217;m doing okay on the engagement side, but I know it&#8217;s time to take it to the next level, which means reaching out more proactively. </p>
<p>It&#8217;s quite exciting how things keep on changing online, but engagement is like an anchor because, unless robots will take over the internet, we&#8217;re dealing with people.</p>
<p>Have a great week ahead of you, my friend!</p>
<p>&#8211; Jasper</p>

They won&#8217;t however be able to carry on a real conversation and people will start figuring that out which could end up being a total disaster but I&#8217;m thinking they just want to get the conversation started because that&#8217;s the direction we have to go.</p>

				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>Such a great point you made here. Even when some of us sort of *know* this to be true, it&#8217;s so good to be reminded of it once in a while. Why? because it&#8217;s SO EASY to start obsessing over numbers again! lol</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve been covering web trends for Aboutcom for five years now, and because it&#8217;s such a massive site that has a lot of authority with Google, we&#8217;ve always been all about the big numbers (a.k.a. the page views). Every writer who covers a topic there gets loads of page views, but do people stick around? Not really. I mean, there&#8217;s been some slow improvement with it, but engagement has always been a big issue site-wide with About and now we can&#8217;t afford to ignore it because Google is starting to use these types of metrics in its rankings. Big changes are come for to the site this year, and while I&#8217;m excited, I&#8217;m also a bit terrified that it&#8217;s kind of too little, too late. I have a lot of faith in the super talented team we have working on SEO and social and design and everything, but the internet changes so fast these days and About has always been several steps behind. I&#8217;m hoping this is the year we can turn it around and get back up to speed with where we should be for 2016 and beyond. But, you know, we can&#8217;t just start pretending to be BuzzFeed to do all that. 😛</p>
<p>Thanks for the great article and reminder, Adrienne!</p>
<p>Elise</p>

<p>Yes, I do remember the days when Page Rank, how many unique visitors you had coming to your blog, and how many page views you were getting were what mattered. You are absolutely right. It is the engagement that now matters the most and what we do with that engagement &#8211; not the traffic numbers. Having those one-on-one conversations with someone is golden.</p>
<p>Thank you for another value-packed post! I will be sharing this <img src="http://www.adriennesmith.net/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
<p>Have a wonderful week, my friend!<br />

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi, Adrienne,</p>
<p>Trust me, Adrienne, with so much to learn and the ever changing trend in blogging, it’s a miracle truckloads of us are still committed to this anyway. But the good thing about it, like James McAllister once pointed out in his post, is to figure this out: why do you blog? Why do get your bum up everyday, park it before some laptop to crank out texts that would most likely not be read a fraction of 2000 people? </p>
<p>Why? </p>
<p>Because you love to do it? Because it’s all about the money? Because you want to be the next Seth Godin? </p>
<p>Truth is, overtime, your true “why” begins to show, and it helps you to hold on or fizzle. So I’ve found the strongest “why” that would keep a blogger going is the one that’s centered around reaching out to people, adding tremendous value to them, connecting like “what in the world”, and of course, you’ve got to make money blogging, too, or you’ll soon be frustrated out of it. </p>
<p>So, yes, this is what we ought to be doing from the onset: deepening connection with the targeted visitors. And I just love that you have a done great justice to this topic. </p>
<p>My question though is, Adrienne, do you think this trend would take a different turn? How soon? And how should we be prepared for it?</p>
<p><b> &#8211; Yusuff Busayo</b><b></p>

				<p>Hi Yusuff,</p>
<p>People blog for so many different reasons.  For the budding entrepreneurs though they are here building their businesses.  So blogging for them is of course trying to get their content in front of as many of the right people as possible so that they&#8217;ll want to take action and hopefully that will start by either commenting on their posts or emailing the author.  Either way when you are in business for yourself it&#8217;s crucial to make those connections because those are the people who will either buy from you or support what you do.  Building a community is SO important because we all need support, we all need those people who are there to help spread the word about us.  </p>
<p>I&#8217;m not sure what you mean by will this trend take a different turn!  Numbers are important but only when they are the right audience.  People are more impressed when they come to a blog and see actual conversations taking place.  Sure, the social shares are great because it means people like your content and are sharing it too but it gives people a certain sense that you know what you&#8217;re talking about.  That will help make that connection to the next step even easier because the trust factor is already starting to build.</p>

				<p>Hi Andrew,</p>
<p>Thank you, I appreciate that.</p>
<p>As with all predictions and trends that come out, just like with blog commenting and blogging being dead, those are just things that people think may or may not happen.  I understand that people do like to comment and share their thoughts but their predictions are that they&#8217;ll do them other places than our blogs.  That may or may not be true for a lot of people but the key point here is that there are conversations taking place and we need to be sure we&#8217;re having them as well.  </p>
<p>When people do come to our blogs it&#8217;s of course up to us to grab their attention with our awesome content, make them feel welcome, solve the problem which is why they stopped by, but also make an honest connection with them.  Sure, it might not be the first time or the second but I would hope that it would.  We need to be sure that we&#8217;re taking this conversation elsewhere as well but it does start on our blogs.  It&#8217;s about community and that&#8217;s something I&#8217;ve been saying for years.  It&#8217;s just becoming much more evident as time goes by and of course you&#8217;re very aware of this as well.</p>
<p>I miss you Andrew, blogging that is.  I so appreciate you stopping by and commenting of course but I&#8217;m eager to see what you do with your blog and the direction that you head.  I know it will be awesome my friend.  I&#8217;m here if you need any advice.  😉</p>
<p>Thank you so much and you enjoy the rest of your day as well as your week.  I intend to do the same.</p>

			<div class="comment_area">
				
				<div class="comment-content clearfix">
				<p>Hi Adrienne,</p>
<p>AS we know, numbers aren&#8217;t everything. Are they?</p>
<p>I just met a highly successful entrepreneur who is driving mega traffic to his site. The problem is no one is filing out the forms, calling or coming to his place of business saying they were on his site.</p>
<p>The problem was he is driving all the wrong traffic.</p>
<p>His message is non-existent and he&#8217;s just screaming &#8220;buy me&#8221; and of course they are not.</p>
<p>Now he&#8217;s working on identifying what business he is &#8220;really&#8221; in and is focusing specifically on the problems he&#8217;s passionate about solving so that he focus on driving the &#8220;right&#8221; traffic to his website. </p>
<p>Personally, I just got approved for syndication on business2community.com and The Huffington Post. I&#8217;m also working on Entrepreneur.com, Forbes.com and Business.com.</p>
<p>All highly targeted, relevant websites.</p>
<p>While I want a lot of traffic, I want the right targeted traffic and it&#8217;s our message that ultimately delivers that.</p>
<p>Thanks for sharing your ideas around this extremely important issue.</p>
<p>I look forward to our time together on Friday Adrienne!!!</p>
<p>In the meantime, I hope you have an awesome week.</p>
<p>~ Don Purdum<br />

				<p>Hi Harleena,</p>
<p>Happy Monday to you as well and I hope you&#8217;ve had a wonderful day so far.</p>
<p>Numbers are awesome if you&#8217;re getting your desired results from them.  You&#8217;ll never get them from everyone but if the majority of the traffic that hits your site is taking the action you wanted then you should brag.  Lets face it though, 99.9% of those people aren&#8217;t getting those results.  That&#8217;s what we were taught though.  There are more and more people coming online today so we have to stand out, grab their attention and make a difference.  We have to make that personal connection with them and start that relationship.  If people aren&#8217;t doing this now then they&#8217;re going to be behind.  We all need to step this up because that&#8217;s the way to build your business.</p>
<p>I always appreciate your comment Harleena, thank you so much for stopping by today.</p>
<p>Yes, I&#8217;ve been trying to decide how to &#8220;brand&#8221; my images and I worked on that this weekend and found what I love so I&#8217;ve redone all the images from the first of the year and will be consistent moving forward.  Thank you, glad you like them.  It&#8217;s only taken me forever to make up my darn mind.  LOL!!</p>
<p>You have a wonderful week now.</p>
